### SOURCE.md ai-jail → macOS: granular adaptation (opened `20260713.211800`, first landed `20260714.052900`)

*Cursor ships as a native `.app` on macOS with a `cursor` CLI wrapper (Homebrew-installed, confirmed on this Mac) — no AppImage, no `squashfs-root/AppRun`. The `--user-data-dir` / `--extensions-dir` flags `tools/cursor-jail.sh` already relies on exist unchanged in the macOS build, so the project-local state-directory model ports directly.*

- [x] Author `tools/cursor-jail-macos.sh` — a shell launcher (not yet the Rye/Rishi seed originally proposed; landed as bash first, matching `tools/cursor-jail.sh`'s own POSIX-seam precedent) that generates an SBPL `(deny default)` profile inline and execs `sandbox-exec -f <profile> -- cursor --user-data-dir=... --extensions-dir=... "$REPO"` — [`tools/cursor-jail-macos.sh`](../tools/cursor-jail-macos.sh)
- [x] Witness: `tools/cursor_jail_macos_witness.sh` — **both green on this host** `20260714.052900`: write inside the project succeeds, write outside (to real `$HOME`) is denied with `Operation not permitted`, confirmed with no leaked file
- [x] Guide: [`manual/guides/macos-ai-jail-setup.md`](../manual/guides/macos-ai-jail-setup.md) — the practical setup and troubleshooting path, honest about what is still open
- [x] **Rish-native launcher + witness** — [`tools/cursor_jail_macos.rish`](../tools/cursor_jail_macos.rish) + [`tools/cursor_jail_macos_witness.rish`](../tools/cursor_jail_macos_witness.rish), landed `20260714.060500`; same SBPL profile as the bash elders (`join`/fixture-quote technique for the embedded `"` SBPL needs — a new `tools/fixtures/dquote.txt` one-byte fixture, same shape as the existing `newline.txt`); bash elders kept beside them, not replaced
- [x] **GUI launch actually proven** `20260714.070500` — the first launcher *reported* success while launching nothing (three stacked traps, each silent): (1) the `cursor` CLI wrapper's detached spawn dies under Seatbelt (`bootstrap_check_in` denied) — exec the app binary directly; (2) Chromium's own sandbox cannot nest inside Seatbelt (same law as bwrap on Linux, `SOURCE.md` Step 9) — pass `--no-sandbox`; (3) inherited stdio pipes die with the launcher and Electron takes a `SIGPIPE` seconds later — `nohup` + `/dev/null` redirects. Profile's Mach/IPC/pty section adopted from upstream ai-jail's own new macOS backend. Witness now tests the launcher's emitted profile (one source of truth). Jailed instance verified alive past 35s, fresh signed-out state (login isolation working)
- [x] **Upstream ai-jail went multi-OS** — installed v1.13.0 (macOS aarch64 release binary; the brew tap needs an SSH key so the curl artifact is the documented path), write fence witnessed on this host (inside OK, `$HOME` denied); now first-class here for CLI agents/shells, while our launcher remains the GUI path — gratitude note [`gratitude/20260714-070200_ai-jail-macos-backend.md`](../gratitude/20260714-070200_ai-jail-macos-backend.md)
- [x] Extend `SOURCE.md` Step 6, 7, 8, and Verifying with the macOS variant path — landed `20260714.073300`–`085000`: native Seatbelt launcher, the repo-local `core.sshCommand` fix for a multi-account `IdentitiesOnly` collision, the GPG trustdb-hang quirk, and Step 8's `--harden-home` flow all cross-linked from `manual/guides/macos-ai-jail-setup.md`
- [x] **`--harden-home` built** `20260714.081500` — denies reads to a named list of real credential stores under `$HOME` (`~/.ssh`, `~/.gnupg`, `~/.aws`, `~/.config/gh`, and the rest), leaving every other read open; discovered Seatbelt on this host resolves an overlapping allow/deny pair to **deny regardless of order or specificity**, so the design is a deny-only named list, not a blanket-deny-with-allow-back. `tools/generate_jail_local_keys_macos.rish` mints dedicated, jail-only SSH + GPG keys from an ordinary terminal outside any jail, reading identity from `GLOW_PROFILE.bron`; `tools/cursor_jail_macos_harden_witness.rish` proves the deny list, with an honest, named limit — it cannot self-certify from inside an already-jailed window (a nested `sandbox_apply` carrying a `deny` rule fails outright on this host)
- [x] **Jail-local identity fixed and verified on both forges** `20260714.085000`–`093300` — the first-minted GPG key had no email (would never show Verified); corrected in place (fingerprint preserved) to carry the real name/handle/email; SSH and GPG keys verified via Codeberg's and GitHub's own challenge-signature flow
- [x] **`gh` under `--harden-home`** — denies `~/.config/gh` by design; documented scoped-`GH_TOKEN` + jail-local `GH_CONFIG_DIR` path in `SOURCE.md` Step 8d and the guide, so `gh` works without the real broad token ever entering the jail (Keaton's own token to mint, not built here)
- [x] **History rewrite, verified clean** `20260714.093300` — 87 of Keaton's own commits (the true fork point onward, correctly excluding 18 commits from other named Urbit contributors) re-signed with the jail-local key via `git filter-branch`'s commit-filter; byte-diffed against a backup before pushing (author/committer/dates/messages all identical, only the signature changed); force-pushed with `--force-with-lease` to `codeberg`/`github` only, `upstream-urbit-foundation` untouched
- [x] Standalone SVG QR codes beside the PNG key card — `tools/make_key_qr_svg.rish`, `20260714.114000`
- [x] A scoped Radiant Style sweep over this tree's 85 living, first-party docs (7 root, 11 `context/`, 15 `manual/`, ~20 module READMEs) — dated archives and the `strengthening-compiler/` spec catalog explicitly out of scope; found and fixed 7 real "but" instances, confirmed the tree already well-kept
- [ ] Network egress *filtering* (proxy-based, allow-list by host) — the current script only offers allow-all or deny-all
- [x] Fold the `known_hosts` finding (`--harden-home` also breaks SSH host-key verification) into the tooling itself — `20260714.183000`: `tools/generate_jail_local_keys_macos.rish` now creates a jail-local `known_hosts` and wires git automatically; `tools/cursor_jail_macos_harden_witness.rish` checks it mechanically
- [x] **`--private-home` built** `20260714.190500` — a full private-`$HOME` equivalent: denies every top-level real `$HOME` entry except the project's own directory, enumerated fresh at each launch. The scoping doc's own first design (a scratch `$HOME` with curated symlinks) turned out fatal on this host: the project lives *inside* the real `$HOME`, and Seatbelt's proven deny-always-wins-an-overlap rule means a blanket deny would have denied the project too. The shipped shape sidesteps that entirely by never denying the project's path in the first place. Combines freely with `--harden-home`. Witnessed by `tools/cursor_jail_macos_private_home_witness.rish` (same outside-the-jail self-testing limit). One named incompleteness: a symlinked `$HOME` entry is denied by its own literal path, not its resolved target, so a symlink pointing outside `$HOME` can still leak through
- [x] Two new Rish language-gap fixtures discovered and added — `tools/fixtures/backslash.txt` (a literal `\` character; Rish strings have no backslash escapes at all, not just no `\"`)
- [ ] Extend `context/specs/enclosure-editors.md` with a macOS section alongside the existing Ubuntu/NixOS ones
- [ ] A full vector (SVG) rebuild of the composited key card, replacing the ImageMagick raster pipeline — named as a real, separate project, not attempted
- [ ] A Radiant Style pass over `strengthening-compiler/`'s prose sections — needs its own scoping pass first (the catalog is mostly structured technical spec, not narrative)
- Session log: [`session-logs/20260713-201910_local-fork-pass1-restructure.bron`](../session-logs/20260713-201910_local-fork-pass1-restructure.bron); today's full thread from [`session-logs/20260714-072700_ai-jail-write-fence-witnessed-live.bron`](../session-logs/20260714-072700_ai-jail-write-fence-witnessed-live.bron) through [`session-logs/20260714-114000_tidying_and_radiant_sweep.bron`](../session-logs/20260714-114000_tidying_and_radiant_sweep.bron)

Collision research: Riyo/Trey quiet; Triz a low-stakes TRIZ soft-collision; Reya collides with ReyaChain and this fork's own retired Reya 2 voice.

- [x] **Pool keystone revival — prioritized `20260715.172000`, ladder fully closed `20260715.205500`** — named as the single most load-bearing Urbit-vane revival for Glow: Gall's userspace-host role, revived as Pool, with **Realidream** as its Landscape-parallel viewer. Ames/Clay already live (Comlink/Mantra green), identity half-lives (Kumara); Pool is the host that turns the green spine into a system a person can inhabit, and every product-layer concern (Linengrow, Open Asks, sanctuary care log, content market, Greencandy) is Gall-shaped. Composes Caravan's supervision + capability table rather than starting cold. Decision brief: [`../external-research/20260715-172000_pool-keystone-revival-realidream-landscape.md`](../external-research/20260715-172000_pool-keystone-revival-realidream-landscape.md). Ladder (**all four rungs GREEN — P0·P1·R1·R2**, unblocking the Sala B1/B2 broadcast lane below):
  - [x] **P0 — Pool host seam** — **GREEN `20260715.201500`**: [`../linengrow/pool_host_seam.rye`](../linengrow/pool_host_seam.rye) hosts one agent over Caravan's *own* capability table (`caravan/capabilities.rye`, imported real — its query surface made `pub` additively, Caravan witness stays green); admission is a capability check (`allows(agent, resource, right)`), not a name check; the agent's state is a verified MALA fold. Witness proves five claims (granted agent admitted + folds; ungranted refused `NotAdmitted`; read-only refused — exact right checked; two hostings agree bit-for-bit; tampered log refused `FoldFailed`). First tenant a minimal ledger agent standing in for the closed Open Ask loop (the P1 tenant). Wired into `tools/parity_ch01.rish` via `tools/pool_host_seam_witness.rish`. **Unblocks Sala B1 (live carriage) and the R-rungs.**
  - [x] **P1 — two agents, one capability boundary** — **GREEN `20260715.202500`**: [`../linengrow/pool_isolation_witness.rye`](../linengrow/pool_isolation_witness.rye) (on `pool_host_seam.host_agent_on`, added additively) proves two Pool agents, each owning its own state resource in Caravan's table, cannot touch each other's state without a named grant. Five claims: each folds its own independent state (issuer 200 vs 250); agent-a refused at agent-b's state and vice-versa (mutual isolation); an explicit grant is the *only* bridge that opens cross-access; and that grant does not leak the other way. Wired into `tools/parity_ch01.rish` via `tools/pool_isolation_witness.rish`.
  - [x] **R1 — Realidream first view over Pool** — **GREEN `20260715.204500`**: [`../linengrow/sala_view.rye`](../linengrow/sala_view.rye) renders a Pool-hosted agent's folded state as a bounded frame (the thin-view exception, sourced from a real Pool `AgentResult`, not a local fixture — Pool hosts, Sala shows). [`../linengrow/sala_view_witness.rye`](../linengrow/sala_view_witness.rye) proves four claims: the frame reflects the fold (real balances appear), rendering is deterministic (same state → byte-identical frame), the frame is bounded (≤8 lines, ≤64 cols — thin-view), and only what Pool hosts is rendered (a refused agent leaves nothing to show). Wired into `tools/parity_ch01.rish` via `tools/sala_view_witness.rish`.
  - [x] **R2 — Realidream as the unified viewer** — **GREEN `20260715.205500`**: [`../linengrow/sala_surface.rye`](../linengrow/sala_surface.rye) gathers many capability-isolated Pool-hosted agents (ask · receipt · reputation) onto one bounded Sala surface, each rendered as its own fold — the Landscape-parallel proper. [`../linengrow/sala_surface_witness.rye`](../linengrow/sala_surface_witness.rye) proves four claims: three isolated agents render as three panels each reflecting its distinct fold (issuer 200/250/275); two surfaces from the same states agree byte-for-byte; the surface is bounded (≤8 panels); and only Pool-hosted agents earn a panel (an ungranted `sanctuary` agent is refused and shows nothing). Wired into `tools/parity_ch01.rish` via `tools/sala_surface_witness.rish`. **This closes the Pool keystone ladder (P0·P1·R1·R2 all green) and is the second thin-view consumer that graduates Dexter.**

- [x] **Real bug caught and fixed: HAWM0's own boot worker killed the emulator it just proved GREEN** `20260716.140207` — Keaton hit this live on the host: `tools/hawm0_boot_onpath_host.rish` printed a clean GREEN close (twice, in fact — model=`sdk_gphone64_x86_64`, `boot_completed` in ~1s the second time), then `tools/hawm1_sala_witness.rish` immediately reported "no emulator attached." Root cause: `tools/hawm0_boot_worker.sh` set `trap cleanup EXIT` to tear the emulator down on any script exit, including the ordinary successful one at the very end — so every "successful" boot silently killed its own device a moment after proving it worked, before anything downstream (HAWM1's own `adb push`) could ever attach. Fixed by disarming the trap (`trap - EXIT`) immediately before the GREEN close; only a real failure path (boot never reaches `sys.boot_completed`, `adb` never attaches, etc.) still tears the emulator down automatically. Added [`tools/hawm0_stop.sh`](../tools/hawm0_stop.sh) — the explicit, on-purpose teardown for when a booted `hawm0` is actually no longer wanted, since the boot script itself no longer self-terminates on success. The correct sequence going forward, in the same terminal session: boot `hawm0`, then run `hawm1_sala_witness.rish` while it is still up, then `hawm0_stop.sh` when actually done
- [x] **Second bug, caught the very next run: the boot script's own "already attached" guard now fails a healthy re-run** `20260716.141522` — the trap fix above worked exactly as designed (Keaton's second `hawm0_boot_onpath_host.rish` call found the still-running emulator from the first), yet an older guard in `tools/hawm0_boot_worker.sh`, written back when every run self-terminated, treated *any* already-attached emulator as `RED: an emulator is already attached — close it first`, with no check for whether it was actually healthy. This made an ordinary, idempotent second call into the boot script fail for no real reason — exactly the scenario the trap fix was supposed to make routine. Fixed: the guard now reads `sys.boot_completed` on the existing device before deciding — genuinely booted means idempotent GREEN success (reports the same device identity, exits 0, never launches a second competing emulator process against the same AVD); only a truly stuck or offline attachment still refuses, now naming the actual `sys.boot_completed` value in its own RED message. Verified the three real decision branches (fresh launch, healthy re-run, stuck re-run) in an isolated bash unit test against a faked `adb`, all three correct, before trusting the real script's own logic. Also closed a related visibility gap in `tools/hawm0_boot_onpath_host.rish` and `tools/hawm1_sala_witness.rish`: a build or boot failure's real stderr was captured in the run record, yet never printed to the terminal on a RED close — a caller had to dig into gitignored log files to learn why. Both entrypoints now print the captured stderr directly whenever the underlying call fails
- [x] **HAWM1 — GREEN, end to end** `20260716.141946` — Keaton ran `tools/hawm1_sala_witness.rish` for real, both bugfix rounds above holding: the Sala B0 witness, cross-built for `x86_64-linux-android`, ran inside the real, KVM-booted `hawm0` device via `adb push`/`adb shell`, and its on-device session root (`99b3ae967c5a230acfc598a7e949b3c2c638ce996be47a51a7c9f8cb12e4c5fe`) matched the native reference exactly — no divergence. **This closes HAWM1** and is a meaningfully stronger claim than M0's own aarch64/qemu-user result: Glow's fold is now proven correct under Android's real bionic libc, on real hardware acceleration, inside a real device's own userland reached by `adb` — not merely a Linux binary emulated at the CPU level. **HAWM0 and HAWM1 are both real, closed, checkable rungs on the GrapheneOS/Pixel ladder as of this stamp.** The Sala broadcaster app-layer client itself (beyond the B0 core witness) is the next reachable door on this same rung, still horizon; HAWM2 (real GrapheneOS build) and HAWM3 (physical device) remain the only rungs that touch GrapheneOS's own hardening
- [x] **TUBE0 — the Glow app-manifest mold, landed and GREEN** `20260716.145256` — the first concrete, device-free rung of the TUBE application-framework ladder named in [`expanding-prompts/20260716-142818_glow-application-framework-and-publishing.md`](../expanding-prompts/20260716-142818_glow-application-framework-and-publishing.md): [`linengrow/tube_manifest.rye`](../linengrow/tube_manifest.rye) is a bounded manifest value type (name, version, ≥1 declared `DeclaredCapability` reusing `caravan/capabilities.rye`'s own `right_*` bits rather than inventing a parallel set, a real non-zero iteration bound) whose `build()` constructor validates every field before a `Manifest` value can exist at all — the same "checked at expansion, never merely trusted" discipline the rune brief names for a bounded trap's own hidden counter. [`linengrow/tube_manifest_witness.rye`](../linengrow/tube_manifest_witness.rye) proves eight claims (a well-formed manifest builds; `declares()` checks the exact right, not mere resource presence, both for a granted right and a named-but-ungranted one and a never-named resource; five malformed shapes are refused at the manifest's own boundary — empty name, zero declared capabilities, a zero-rights-mask capability, a zero iteration bound). Wired into `tools/parity_ch01.rish` via [`tools/tube0_manifest_witness.rish`](../tools/tube0_manifest_witness.rish); the full chapter reran clean end to end with TUBE0 in place. **A real, pre-existing RED was found during this same full-suite rerun, unrelated to TUBE0**: `tools/tame_style_check.rish` flags a banned `copyForwards` idiom in four files — `linengrow/neth_serial_core.rye` (last touched `20260714.061836`), `sala_session_core.rye`, `sala_surface.rye`, and `sala_view.rye` (all three last touched `20260715`, between `193536` and `194532`) — confirmed via `git log` that none of the four were touched this session; named here honestly rather than silently fixed out of scope, and left for its own dedicated pass

- [x] **No Kotlin transpiler; a native-activity shim named instead** `20260717.014522` — Keaton asked plainly whether Glow should grow a DSL that transpiles to Kotlin for SLC apps, or whether a more TAME-guided, bounded path already exists. Answered in [`active-designing/20260717-014522_native-activity-shim-and-slc-packaging.md`](../active-designing/20260717-014522_native-activity-shim-and-slc-packaging.md): no transpiler — Glow's Android path is already native (Zig → `aarch64-linux-android`/`x86_64-linux-android` bionic ELF, proven bit-identical on HAWM1, HAWM3 pending), and a JVM target would fight TAME's own bounded-loops, no-hidden-allocation, and named-error discipline (GC, unbounded stacks, unchecked exceptions, assertions off by default) for no real gain the rune spec's own bounded `|-` trap doesn't already earn more cheaply on native code. The real gap named honestly: HAWM1/HAWM3 push bare ELF binaries via `adb shell exec`, which proves the fold correct yet is not an installable app — Android/GrapheneOS requires an APK naming a Binder-registered `Activity` before granting an icon, lifecycle, or UI surface. The fix named: one small, fixed, hand-written **native-activity shim** (~50–100 lines, never generated, reused verbatim across every Glow app) handing the window surface across a JNI seam to the Glow-built `.so`, where every rune, bound, and assertion still lives; `linengrow/tube_manifest.rye`'s own GREEN manifest mold becomes the deterministic source for `AndroidManifest.xml` permissions — an assertable emission, never a transpilation. **New rung named: TUBE0.5, "first installable Glow APK on GrapheneOS,"** gated on TUBE0 (GREEN) and HAWM3 (closed) — both gates now closed; the rung itself stays horizon until the shim, the JNI call, and the manifest emission are actually written. Updated `work-in-progress/ROADMAP.md` with the same decision

Recognizes an aura mold (`^-  @u32`, the design brief's own worked example) and a named mold (`^-  record`) alike, ignores a trailing cast expression on the same line without confusing the scan, and refuses three malformed shapes (`NotACast`, `MissingMold`, `MoldNotAnAura` for a mold name that could never legitimately name either shape). [`glow/rune_cast_witness.rye`](../glow/rune_cast_witness.rye) proves six claims, GREEN; wired into `tools/parity_ch01.rish` via [`tools/rune_cast_witness.rish`](../tools/rune_cast_witness.rish), placed directly after the bounded-trap witness it extends. **Still no general Glow parser or lowering pass** — both rune front-ends stay small, named prototypes for exactly one rune's own head each, per their own stated scope discipline; the honest gap named in `expanding-prompts/20260716-142818` stands unchanged Setup chain behind it, landed `20260716.131010` — everything short of the actual KVM boot, all done from inside the jail since none of it needs `/dev/kvm` (only network + disk): fetched and sha256-verified a portable Temurin 21 JDK (`adoptium.net`'s own API) and the Android command-line tools (revision 22.0, sha1-verified against Google's own `repository2-3.xml`), both staged under `tools/.cache/hawm0/` (gitignored, extending the `tools/.cache/proven-seat/` precedent); accepted all SDK licenses non-interactively; installed `platform-tools` 37.0.0, `emulator` 36.6.11, `platforms;android-36`, and `system-images;android-36;google_apis;x86_64` (5.5G, the current stable API with a real x86_64 Google-APIs image — checked directly via `sdkmanager --list` rather than guessing a version); created one AVD named `hawm0`. Hit and worked around a real upstream `avdmanager` bug (22.0's `--device` flag looks for a `devices.xml` at a path the package never ships, for every named device including plain `pixel`) by creating with the generic default profile, then hand-editing `config.ini` to the real, checked Pixel 10 Pro XL panel spec (1344×2992, 486 PPI, 560 logical-density bucket matching other real Pixel-Pro-class AVD skins, 4G RAM) — the flagship device this fork's own go-to-market brief names first. Smoke-tested the `emulator` binary directly (`-version`, no KVM needed) to confirm every shared library resolves before handing off. Converted from a bare shell script to a Rish entrypoint over a bash worker `20260716.132100` — [`tools/hawm0_boot_onpath_host.rish`](../tools/hawm0_boot_onpath_host.rish) asserts `/dev/kvm` + the staged JDK/emulator/AVD, then calls [`tools/hawm0_boot_worker.sh`](../tools/hawm0_boot_worker.sh) (Rish's own `run` is blocking-only, no `&`/`trap`/`wait`/sleep-poll, so the actual backgrounded boot stays in bash, mirroring `tools/lane_kvm_onpath_host.rish`'s own split with `tools/proven_seat_g0c_lane_kvm.sh`). Never touches `tools/lane_kvm.sh` or the ai-jail wall at all — HAWM0 never runs inside the jail in the first place, so there was nothing to widen. **Then run for real, GREEN, `20260716.132659`** — see the bullet above

#### The Neth build ladder — siloed from the IronBeetle stream (`20260714.041542`)

*Patterns from watching a single-threaded, deterministic, append-only, replicated state machine be built in the open, siloed into our own goals and merged here. Full study: [`../external-research/20260714-041542_ironbeetle-patterns-for-the-neth-ladder.md`](../external-research/20260714-041542_ironbeetle-patterns-for-the-neth-ladder.md). Each lap is provable before the next; all gated after the deterministic-root witness (already green).*

- [x] **Neth deterministic-root witness** — green Plan A: two replicas, one signed log, one reproducible root, tamper refused (`linengrow/neth_root_witness.rye`; suite entry in `tools/parity_ch01.rish`).
- [x] **Neth lap — small serial core** — landed `20260714.061500`: [`linengrow/neth_serial_core.rye`](../linengrow/neth_serial_core.rye) (`append_and_reroot`, bounded at `max_append_bytes = 768`, far under `receipt_core.max_log_len`'s 4096) + [`linengrow/neth_serial_core_witness.rye`](../linengrow/neth_serial_core_witness.rye) — two independent calls agree bit-for-bit on the new root; an oversized record is refused with `StepTooLarge` before it ever touches the log (log left byte-for-byte untouched); Comlink carriage, disk write, and record signing are named in the module doc comment and in the witness's own printed record as living outside the call. Wired into the living suite at [`tools/parity_ch01.rish`](../tools/parity_ch01.rish). Standalone GREEN on this host via `tools/neth_serial_core_witness.rish`; the full sequential `parity_ch01.rish` run still halts earlier at the pre-existing, already-named SLC-2a Lap 1 Wayland gap (macOS-only limitation, not a regression from this lap).
- [x] **Neth lap — two-posture root install** — landed `20260715.055500`, **confirmed GREEN on a raised cloud sandbox** `20260715.062000`: [`linengrow/neth_root_install.rye`](../linengrow/neth_root_install.rye) (`install_at_source` trusts the issuing monarch's own current-view root outright, no chain proof demanded; `install_on_repair` admits a peer's root only if it hash-chains onto the last held root; both share one `RootTruncated` rule that refuses any seq behind or ahead of the next expected slot) + [`linengrow/neth_root_install_witness.rye`](../linengrow/neth_root_install_witness.rye) (five claims: ordered trust-at-source install, chain-verified repair install, a wrong-chain repair refused, an already-committed seq refused even under trust-at-source, and trust-at-source's own honest boundary — it admits a non-chain-derived root at the next seq, since it checks ordering, never chain content). Wired into the living suite at [`tools/parity_ch01.rish`](../tools/parity_ch01.rish) via [`tools/neth_root_install_witness.rish`](../tools/neth_root_install_witness.rish).
- [x] **Cloud-agent toolchain raise** — a Cursor Cloud Agent's own disposable Linux sandbox has no `vendor/zig-toolchain/` (gitignored, Mac-host-built only per `GLOW_HOST.bron`); found and confirmed the `pip install ziglang==0.16.0` recipe an earlier Cursor for iOS round already used once against a persistent host (`work-in-progress/20260703-021412_counsel-and-confirmation-tests.md` Step 1) raises `rye`/`rishi` on a fresh cloud VM too — all three Neth witnesses ran real GREEN on it, the first time any Neth witness has run outside a Mac-hosted or Ubuntu-desktop sitting. Written up as its own guide, honest about the different trust chain (PyPI packaging, not the checksum-verified official-release fetch) and what it does not set up (no ai-jail — unneeded on an already-disposable sandbox; no Wayland dev headers) — [`manual/guides/cloud-agent-toolchain-setup.md`](../manual/guides/cloud-agent-toolchain-setup.md)
- [x] **Neth lap — apply-step crash safety** — landed and **confirmed GREEN on the cloud sandbox** `20260715.070000`: [`linengrow/neth_apply_step.rye`](../linengrow/neth_apply_step.rye) (`write_root` lands a root somewhere real but invisible; `apply_pending` is the distinct, later step that admits it into `applied_root` — the one field `consulted()` is ever allowed to read; `recover_after_crash` discards any pending write outright rather than guessing whether it was meant to apply, leaving a prior applied root untouched) + [`linengrow/neth_apply_step_witness.rye`](../linengrow/neth_apply_step_witness.rye) (four claims: a written-but-unapplied root stays invisible, `apply_pending` makes it visible and only then, a crash in the write-to-apply window costs nothing — the prior root stays authoritative and the discarded write redoes and applies cleanly afterward — and applying with nothing pending is refused rather than silently accepted). Wired into the living suite at [`tools/parity_ch01.rish`](../tools/parity_ch01.rish) via [`tools/neth_apply_step_witness.rish`](../tools/neth_apply_step_witness.rish).
- [x] **Neth horizon — deterministic simulation, lap 1** — landed and **confirmed GREEN on the cloud sandbox** `20260715.140000`, after the real replica laps above: [`linengrow/neth_sim.rye`](../linengrow/neth_sim.rye) — a seeded PRNG drives a per-record delivery schedule (a bounded run of drop-then-retry ticks) over `neth_serial_core.rye`'s own already-witnessed `append_and_reroot` fold; scope named honestly — delivery *order* stays fixed by the log itself (Neth's own load-bearing claim, proven elsewhere), the seed varies only *when* each record lands, never its order or content, and an always-dropping seed trips a named `LivenessFailure` bound rather than looping forever. [`linengrow/neth_sim_witness.rye`](../linengrow/neth_sim_witness.rye) proves four claims: the same seed replays a byte-for-byte identical delivery trace and final root on two independent replicas (determinism itself); a genuinely different seed produces a visibly different trace yet still converges on the same final root (safety-under-fault); a 100%-drop seed trips `LivenessFailure` on the first record with nothing applied (the bound enforced, not assumed); and a zero-fault baseline matches every faulted run's root. Wired into [`tools/parity_ch01.rish`](../tools/parity_ch01.rish) via [`tools/neth_sim_witness.rish`](../tools/neth_sim_witness.rish). **This closes the Neth build ladder's every named lap and horizon** from `external-research/20260714-041542_ironbeetle-patterns-for-the-neth-ladder.md` — small serial core, two-posture root install, apply-step crash safety (Neth and its Mantra sibling), and this simulation lap all stand real-GREEN.
- [x] **Neth serial core, carried for real over Comlink** — landed and **confirmed GREEN on the cloud sandbox** `20260715.150000`: every earlier Neth witness named Comlink carriage as "living outside this call," assumed real, never exercised — [`linengrow/neth_serial_core_delivery.rye`](../linengrow/neth_serial_core_delivery.rye) closes that gap for real. A follower replica receives one already-signed record over a genuine hosted UDP hop, sealed under `wire_format.rye` (the same primitive Mantra's recall delivery family and `mala_delivery.rye` already use), and applies it through `neth_serial_core.rye`'s already-witnessed `append_and_reroot` unmodified. **One real, honest bound surfaced and named while building this**: the log's own hex on-disk line comfortably fits `receipt_core`'s 768-byte append bound, yet does not fit Comlink's 340-byte sealed-datagram ceiling — a single hop is smaller than a single log append. Carried the record over the wire in `receipt_core`'s existing compact binary payload instead (raw signature + raw fact, the same encoding `mala_delivery.rye` already uses), reconstructing the log's own hex line only on the receiving side — keeping the wire's compactness concern and the log's stable-shape concern honestly separate. `run_selftest` proves carriage-transparency (sealed-then-opened folds identically to the direct in-process call) and a tamper-refusal at open; `demo` spawns two real subprocesses talking over actual UDP sockets and confirms the follower's carried root matches the source's own independently-computed expectation. Wired into [`tools/parity_ch01.rish`](../tools/parity_ch01.rish) via [`tools/neth_serial_core_delivery_witness.rish`](../tools/neth_serial_core_delivery_witness.rish).

[`mantra/bolt_apply_step_witness.rye`](../mantra/bolt_apply_step_witness.rye) proves five claims against the real namespace law (not an internal stand-in): written-but-unapplied stays `.never`/len-0 to the real `recall`, apply makes it `.here` with the real bytes, a crash costs nothing and the redo applies cleanly, a pending leaf that would violate `RevisionOutOfOrder` is refused exactly as `append_leaf` itself would refuse it (this module adds no admission rule of its own), and applying with nothing pending is refused. Wired into [`tools/parity_ch01.rish`](../tools/parity_ch01.rish) via [`tools/mantra_bolt_apply_step_witness.rish`](../tools/mantra_bolt_apply_step_witness.rish).

  - [x] **The dec jet — fast, slow, and dispatched, proven to agree** `20260716.080000` — Glow's first real jet, per the runes-scoping study's own jet proposal ("every jet in Glow ships with a paired witness — a fixture proving the accelerated path and the pure Glow path produce identical output on the same input"). `slow_dec_formula()` hand-builds a genuinely self-recursive Nock core (composed from opcodes 6, 7, 9, and 10 — exactly the shape Hoon's own `\|-` trap desugars to, built from raw opcodes rather than through any rune or parser); `fast_dec()` is the native O(1) counterpart; `eval_with_dec_jet()` recognizes one hint tag and substitutes the fast path, falling through correctly to the slow path on any other tag. Seven claims include `dec(0)`'s honest refusal two ways (the fast path names it directly; the slow path would loop forever, caught cleanly by `DepthExceeded` rather than hanging) and the interpreter's own depth limit, *measured* (comfortably serves through n=10) rather than guessed. Wired into `tools/parity_ch01.rish` via [`tools/nock_jet_dec_witness.rish`](../tools/nock_jet_dec_witness.rish) — [`nock/nock_jet_dec.rye`](../nock/nock_jet_dec.rye), [`nock/JET_DEC.md`](../nock/JET_DEC.md)
  - [x] **Nock interpreter, lap 3 — the edit primitive and opcode 10** `20260716.070000` — closes the one door lap 2 left open. `edit()` (`#[axis value tree]`) is the constructive counterpart to `slot()`'s own tree addressing: same bit-walk, same address convention, but recorded on the way down (each level's untouched sibling) and rebuilt on the way up, splicing the new value in at exactly the addressed leaf. Bounded by a `u64` axis's own width alone — no separate ceiling, no recursion, two plain loops, honoring TAME root rule 2 even more directly than eval/eql's own depth counter. Opcode 10's two forms (the bare-atom hint, and the real edit `*[a 10 [b c] d] = #[b *[a c] *[a d]]`) dispatch end to end from real formula text, proven equal both to a direct `edit()` call and to an independent, hand-built reconstruction of the official rule. With this lap, **opcodes 0 through 11 — the whole of Nock's own numbered core — are real.** Caught and fixed a genuine regression along the way: implementing opcode 10 accidentally deleted the existing opcode-11 case during editing, caught immediately by rebuilding and rerunning lap 2 rather than assuming it still held. Wired into `tools/parity_ch01.rish` via [`tools/nock_lap3_witness.rish`](../tools/nock_lap3_witness.rish) — [`nock/nock_lap3_witness.rye`](../nock/nock_lap3_witness.rye)
  - [x] **The bounded `|-` rune's front half — a real parser** — closes the one gap the sameness-and-the-rune brief named plainly ("what remains unbuilt is only the front half"). Parses both stated bound shapes (`|-  32` and `|-  (lent records)`), refuses three malformed inputs by name (`NotATrap`, `MissingBound`, `MalformedBoundExpr`), and feeds the extracted bound through the exact counter-checked mechanism the brief's own RISC-V section already quoted from real disassembly — proving welcome and unwelcome paths, end to end, text to mechanism. Wired into `tools/parity_ch01.rish` via [`tools/rune_bounded_trap_witness.rish`](../tools/rune_bounded_trap_witness.rish) — [`glow/rune_bounded_trap.rye`](../glow/rune_bounded_trap.rye), [`glow/rune_bounded_trap_witness.rye`](../glow/rune_bounded_trap_witness.rye)

- [x] **Consumer-surface protection audit (`060112`)** — the innocent surfaces walked for user protection. **What held:** Open Asks consent is opt-in, self-sovereign, non-overwritable (applicant's own key only, post-completion only, set-once, explicit-grant-only counting, `.none`==`.withhold`==excluded — silence means privacy); civic sight displays aggregates only with `withheld=excluded` visible; Granary sharing is explicit-signed-act only; input glass bounded (400B, silent-refuse correct for typed input); Steep design already privacy-leaning (named peers, no open swarm). **Gap found + closed:** the fetch-by-digest wire (`resin_serve_delivery.rye`) served ANY digest without consulting the registry — digest-as-capability; exposed nothing today (store held only published resins) yet sat one step from a real leak since digests travel into public logs. Fix built + witnessed: `granary_core.rye` gains `digest_is_published` + `serve_resin_published` (+ `error.NotPublished`); both wire paths (selftest round-trip AND live UDP demo host) now gate on the published set; new unwelcome path proves an unpublished resin in the same store is refused over the wire; witness asserts `unpublished digest refused` so parity (line 714) guards it permanently. All GREEN on bench. **Principle seated in code comment:** a digest is an address for verifying content, never a capability for reaching it. Counsel `060112`.
- [x] **Steep design-stage note (`060112`)** — seated in living [`steep.md`](../active-designing/steep.md) (`071405`): serving side gates on *pieces explicitly offered to that named peer*, never *any digest the local store holds*; Granary `serve_resin_published` is the precedent.

- [x] **Cursor-bot arc audit (`053412`)** — audited tips 379→430 (PRs #85–#112). **Money code sound:** `linengrow/mala_core.rye` conservation traced by hand — mint is issuer-only (double-guarded: `from`==issuer AND sig verifies against issuer key, holder cannot mint), send strictly conserves (debit-then-credit, underflow-refused); MALA M1 witness GREEN on bench. Naming discipline held (every new module — Granary/Mandi/Greencandy/Anvil/Steep — has a dated seating spec); symlink hygiene held (5 `mala_core.rye` copies all symlink to one canonical, byte-identical); WOV well-witnessed (exit-honesty, TB-pin, host-seam, dual-monarch all in parity). **Fix done + verified, not just recommended:** split three over-length WOV money functions — `publish_root` (72→32), `publish_root_dual` (73→36), `accept_exit_dual` (74→68) — via three shared leaf helpers (`build_attested_bundle`, `write_root_memo`, `append_signed_line`); both WOV witnesses GREEN against refactored code, confirming behavior-preserving. **Left for next hand (named honestly):** `wov_core.rye:run_selftest` (77, test scaffold) and `open_asks_lap5_delivery.rye:run_poster` (73, older orchestration) — stopped at core money-path functions rather than refactor code unverifiable in one pass. *This is the living, granular plan — the bench where the current laps are shaped. `ROADMAP.md` holds the why and the order; this file holds the what-now. It is **edited in place**: a task is checked when it lands, and the record of how it landed accretes in `../session-logs/`. Checked items are swept to a session log and pruned here when a section grows heavy. What is next lives here; what happened lives there.*
